China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Ships 133

Carry Domestic Mail

▲ Contract Signed with the Post Office

▲ Recovering Extraterritorial Rights and Interests

▲ Designated Areas for Hankou, Guangdong, Tianjin, Ningbo, and Wenzhou

The Shanghai Postal Administration has been sending mail to various parts of the country every day. Wherever there is navigation, it has always been carried by foreign ships for a long time. In recent years, extraterritorial rights and interests have been leaking, resulting in huge losses. Now, General Manager Li of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has signed a contract with the post office to carry mail on behalf of domestic courts, which will be implemented from this month, recovering the right of foreign ships to carry packages. The contract was signed yesterday, and the details of this matter are recorded in detail as follows:

▲ Signing the Contract: The post office has contracts with foreign ships to carry mail, which has always been carried by Taikoo, Jardine, and other ships to various ports in the country. Now, because some of the contracts have expired at the end of June, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, as a state-owned shipping company, is under the same Ministry of Communications as the postal service. Therefore, the new General Manager Li Guojie contacted Mr. Zha Peilin, the Shanghai Postmaster, to discuss the matter of carrying mail. After multiple discussions, both parties believed it was feasible and drafted a contract of 19 articles for carrying mail. After the two parties decided, they have signed it, and the guarantor is Li Jia (omitted).

▲ Designated Postal Routes: The area for carrying mail stipulated in the contract is based on the routes currently operated by China Merchants Steam Navigation Company ships. The postal routes agreed upon by both parties are five in total: (A) The Yangtze River area up to Hankou, with mail loaded six times a week, and about eight ships carrying it; (B) The South China area to Guangdong (Panyu), once a week; (C) The Beiyang area to Tianjin, about three times a week; (D) The Wenzhou area to Yongjia, once a week; (E) The Ningbo area to Yinxian, three times a week.

▲ Postal Fees: The standard for paying fees is based on the area occupied by the mail. It has now been stipulated that the Hankou line will occupy 200 cubic feet per ship each time, with a quarterly fee of 12,600 yuan; the Panyu line will occupy 400 cubic feet, with a quarterly fee of 900 yuan; the Tianjin line will occupy 300 cubic feet, with a quarterly fee of 1,016 yuan; the Yongjia line will occupy 240 cubic feet, with a quarterly fee of 270 yuan; the Yinxian line will occupy 480 cubic feet, with a quarterly fee of 540 yuan.

▲ Implemented on July 1: After the contract was signed, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has notified the ships to set up mail storage rooms on the ships. From July 1, commercial ships on the Yangtze River, Beiyang, and Ningbo-Wenzhou routes have been ordered to start loading. However, it is stipulated that after this mail transportation contract is signed, the ships are not allowed to carry private letters, and after the number of postal runs is stipulated, the shipping schedule and missing runs may not be changed at any time. In the event of special circumstances where the ship cannot operate according to the schedule, the company should give priority to entrusting the mail that should be loaded to other Chinese shipping companies, such as Sanbei, to carry it out to avoid delaying the export of mail.

Overseas Chinese 134

Expelled from Japan After the War

During the January 28th War, overseas Chinese in Japan were insulted by the Japanese and gave up their businesses one after another to return home to avoid the disaster. Now that the war is over, overseas Chinese want to go to Japan to restore their businesses, but they are being rejected by the Japanese and are not allowed to land. In recent days, there have been many cases of Japanese expelling Chinese who went to Japan after the war back to Shanghai. The details are recorded as follows:

▲ Prohibition of Going to Japan: The Japanese rejection of Chinese workers has long become a prominent fact. After the Shanghai War, the Japanese took the opportunity to prohibit overseas Chinese who had already left the East from going again, and ordered various Japanese shipping companies in Shanghai to issue announcements, stating that Chinese going to various ports in Japan must clearly state their detailed address and business when purchasing tickets and bring a certificate of permission to enter the country before they can purchase tickets. Those without a definite address and certificate will not be sold tickets, and please do not go to the East, because the ship ticket will still be paid by the passenger when they are returned due to being prohibited from landing.

▲ Going to the East to Resume Business: Overseas Chinese who returned home during the war left Japan in a hurry and mostly did not apply for a re-entry certificate to go again. Now that the Japanese can freely come to China to resume business, recently overseas Chinese from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Fujian who have businesses in Japan have purchased tickets from the Japanese Post Office to Osaka, Kobe, Nagasaki, and other places to resume their businesses and close their shops. Unexpectedly, many of those who did not have a lamp certificate were not allowed to board the ship, and only those with a guarantee and a permit could go to Japan.

▲ Prohibition of Landing: When these overseas Chinese arrived in Osaka, Kobe, Nagasaki, Nagoya, and other ports, they were not allowed to land by the Japanese water police on the pretext of not having a certificate and were detained in the police station and insulted in every possible way before being escorted back to Shanghai on the original ship. There have been multiple batches of this in the past few days, including Chen Yonghua, Fang Zhuguan, Chen Famin, Yang Taijin, Lin Chihe, Yang Shenggen, Liu Zhenzhang, Jin Laidi, Lin Zaijin, Lin Jia Zhi, Lin Songben, Wang Chunjiu, Lin Xinjing, and more than 30 others were all expelled back to Shanghai, spending money on round-trip travel and watching their shops and property in Japan that they could not go to and move away. Therefore, everyone was extremely angry when they arrived in Shanghai.

Liu Tongsheng Kidnapped by Bandits 135

Intending to Get 20,000 Gold

▲ Wang A'lin and His Mistress Also Captured

▲ The Bandits Confessed to the Kidnapping in Great Detail

Liu Tongsheng, a comprador from Tianna Foreign Company's Western Medicine Department and a native of Jiujiang, was kidnapped by bandits at about 10:00 AM on the 6th in front of the Yijia house at 218 Yuezhou Road and driven to the jurisdiction of the First Branch of the Seventh District of Gao Langqiao Yinxian Township. Because they ran out of gasoline, the members of the local security corps rushed to the scene after hearing the alarm and fought with the bandits, killing a bandit surnamed Zhang. A bandit named Qian Xuen, a native of Tongzhou, was captured on the spot, and a pistol was seized with two bullets inside. The hostage Liu Tongsheng was rescued. After receiving the report, the Huishan Concession Police sent Chinese Detective Lu Gengsheng, Lin Kehsun, and scout Chen Ou Hai to bring the suspect Qian back to the police station. Another accomplice, Ji Jinhua, a native of Tongzhou, was captured at 155 Xinxin Lane, Jin Shenfu Road in the French Concession. It was learned that there was another accomplice, Jiang Jingui, hiding in a house at 1290 Xieji Road in the Chinese territory, and Jiang was arrested at that address and taken to the Municipal Public Security Bureau. The suspect Qian Xuen, Ji Jinhua, and the body of the bandit surnamed Zhang who was killed on the spot were sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and inspection. Subsequently, Detective Lu, who was in charge of the case, etc., captured another accomplice, Wang A'lin (also known as Tang Hongfu and Tang Liancheng), a native of Tongzhou, and a woman named Lu Huangshi at 11 Kangti Road in the French Concession. They were taken to the police station and detained separately. Yesterday morning, Jiang Jingui, who was transferred from the Public Security Bureau, was sent to the Fourth Criminal Court of the Special Court, and Judge Shen Bingrong took the seat for interrogation. The police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated the previous situation and requested that after questioning, the case be postponed and combined with the interrogation of Qian Xuen and others. He also said that two coachmen from Liu Tongsheng's place would be in court to identify them today. According to Xia Qingqi, he has been working as a coachman at Liu's house for five years. When the master was kidnapped at the time, the defendant Wang A'lin was holding a pistol, threatening me loudly, and pushing me down in the car. The master's foot was injured. At the time, I heard a gunshot, but I didn't know who fired it. According to Sun Haitao, the assistant of Xia, at the time I only saw the defendant Qian Xuen, who was being transferred to the court yesterday, holding a pistol. I couldn't identify the others. When asked about Jiang Jingui's testimony, he said that he was a cart puller and knew Qian Xuen as a fellow villager. A week ago, he and a certain Jia came to my house and asked how my current situation was. I said that business was deserted and it was difficult to make a living. He also said that if I worked as a cart puller, I would never get rich. Now there is something. If it is settled, I will come and tell you again and left. The day before yesterday, Qian came again and told me to wait on Baoshan Road at about 9:00 AM to buy (omitted) rice for 10 copper coins and eat my fill. He said that at a certain place, at about 10:30, a car would pass by and he would ask me to help. Unexpectedly, I waited until noon and didn't see anything, so I returned home and was arrested. Qian did not clarify the kidnapping matter. The rest of the testimony was evasive. According to Wang A'lin's testimony, his surname was Tang, named Hongfu. Later, because he was adopted into the Wang family, he changed his name to A'lin and had no other name Liancheng. A friend named Ji Jinhe asked me to have tea in a nearby tea house. He said that there was a cousin Xia Qingqi who was a coachman in a certain family. He knew the details and could make a kidnapping business. He asked me to join. I said that this matter had to do with life and I didn't dare to do it. He said that I didn't need to be timid. There were no police around the house and it could be done. Three days later, he came to my house again and said that the driver and pistol had been found and it could be implemented. The day before the incident, I and Ji Jinhe, Qian Xuen, Ji Jinhua, and the deceased Zhang and others, a total of seven people, took the 18th Road trolleybus at 8:00 AM and got off in front of Liu's house on Yuezhou Road. We played in the middle of the road. At about 10:00 AM, we saw the God of Wealth coming out of the house and getting into a car we had prepared to go to a certain place to do business. We didn't take action that morning. We were recognizing the face of the God of Wealth. The next morning, those who went with me were Ji Jinhua, Qian Xuen, and the deceased Zhang, including myself, a total of four people. We still left at 8:00 AM and took the trolleybus to the front of Liu's house and waited. Ji Jinhe didn't go. At the time, the deceased Zhang first stepped forward and fired a shot to intimidate him, while Ji Jinhua was driving. I pushed Xia Qingqi down into the car. The deceased Zhang and Qian Xuen guarded the God of Wealth. I heard someone say that this matter would definitely get 20,000 gold and be divided into eight shares. Unexpectedly, the incident failed and I escaped home until I was arrested. Lu Huangshi is my mistress. She didn't know about this. According to her, she had only been in Shanghai from Tongzhou for half a month. It is true that she knew Wang (A'lin), but she didn't know anything else. Judge Shen ordered them to be remanded in custody separately and rescheduled to be tried together with Qian Xuen and others.

Tax on Production and Sales in Jiangxi Not Approved by Ministry 136

Jiangxi various industry associations' protest petition group issued a message stating that Jiangxi Province has established a special product production and sales tax, encompassing all imported, exported, locally produced, and locally sold goods, with offices set up everywhere. Its severity surpasses even the Likin tax. Take timber, a major product of Jiangxi, which is crucial to the livelihood of laborers and the province's economic prosperity or decline. For years, those who harvest timber in the mountains have suffered from exploitation by rampant bandits, while those who trade timber outside the province face competition from imported foreign pine. Since the fifteenth year of the Republic (1926), business conditions have plummeted, with most businesses on their last breath, on the verge of collapse. Upon hearing that the provincial government was establishing a production and sales tax, all timber merchants were deeply distressed. They all said that after the numerous disasters, the remaining businesses could not bear the burden of such a harsh, disguised Likin tax. They would inevitably close down, which would affect the millions of laborers who depend on timber for their livelihood. These millions of laborers, suddenly unemployed, would inevitably resort to desperate measures and become bandits. The timber merchants believed that it was necessary to consider these potential consequences, so they resolutely decided to convene all timber businesses in the province, as well as timber guilds in Beijing, Changzhou, and Anhui, and sent a letter to the Nanchang Timber Industry Association, requesting them to convene a joint meeting. It was resolved to petition the provincial government to exempt them from the tax in order to relieve the merchants' difficulties and protect the people's lives, and also to telegraph to various central ministries and departments. Yesterday, it was learned that the Ministry of Finance had issued a reply stating: "National Government Ministry of Finance Express Mail Telegram, Ref. No. 337, Nanchang Timber Industry Association, read. Your winter telegram is noted. The matter of Jiangxi Province establishing a production and sales tax has not been approved by the Ministry. Please be informed, Finance Ministry Seal."

The Shanghai silver and money trade association sent a letter to the Municipal Council expressing its gratitude for the protection provided by the merchant corps during the wartime. Jianghai Customs Burns Confiscated Narcotics 138

The Jianghai Customs Anti-Smuggling Bureau seized a large quantity of contraband narcotics on various ships during the past three months (from December 21 of this year to June 20). Yesterday morning at 8:00 AM, the narcotics were transported to the Guanzhan Wharf in Lujiazui, Pudong, for incineration. Supervisors from various agencies were present, including Jin Yu from the Garrison Headquarters, Huang Chen from the Municipal Government, Lu Youchang from the Supervisory Office, Ju Zhijing from the First Special District Court, Ren Bin from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Wang Yiqian from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, and Yu Baozhen, the district head of the Third District, who dispatched Inspector Liu Zhenya, leading a platoon of armed police officers, to the scene to maintain order. At 9:15 AM, the manager of the Guanzhan, McPherson, ordered the stokers and laborers to weigh and inspect all the narcotics and successively throw them into the kiln for incineration. The incineration was completed at 11:00 AM. The items burned included 20 dan and 68 jin and 9 liang of opium, valued at 82,633.1 yuan in silver; morphine drugs (i.e., red pills, etc.) valued at 8,806.87 yuan in silver; 2 liang of morphine; 50 jin of opium poppy shells; and opium paraphernalia. The total value of the above was estimated at over 91,770 yuan in silver. In addition, several dozen photographs of nude women (i.e., erotic pictures) and eight burlap bags of various contraband items sent by the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession were also incinerated in the kiln. Afterward, Tax Officer Huang Yaochuan invited the supervisors to the reception room of the Customs School for refreshments before dispersing.

Love Wanes When Money Runs Out 139

Five Tendons Severed on Beautiful Woman's Foot

▲ Gu Linsheng's Methods Too Cruel

▲ Sentenced to Eight Months Imprisonment

Du Shen, a woman from Changzhou, 28 years old, had a long-standing affair with Gu Linsheng in her hometown. However, because her husband often interfered, they could not freely express their affection. Therefore, they fled together to Shanghai. The woman stayed with her aunt, Yang Gu, at 799 Zhejiang Road. Gu Linsheng would invite her to a hotel for pleasure every few days. Recently, Gu's finances had become very strained, and the woman began to treat him coldly. The intensity of her love depended entirely on the amount of money he had. This is a common ailment among modern young men and women, and these rural villagers were naturally unable to escape this pattern. Unfortunately, Gu was as foolish as a deer or pig and did not know how to read her face or recognize her emotions. He still clung to her and insisted on seeing her. The night before last, at midnight, he still wanted to invite her for an intimate encounter, but the woman sneered at him. Gu became enraged and left in a huff. Shortly after, he returned with four or five violent men. Gu grabbed a sharp axe and, because the woman had been unwilling to follow him, he hacked at her feet, causing axe wounds to her ankles and the calf of her right foot. Blood flowed freely. Zhang Huisheng and others, who lived with her, restrained Gu, and the others fled in all directions. The Lao Zha Police Station received a report and dispatched Detective Wang Yifei to the scene. The assailant and the weapon were taken to the police station for detention. The injured woman was sent to Renji Hospital, where doctors diagnosed that five tendons in her right foot had been severed. They performed emergency surgery, using fine copper wire to reconnect the severed tendons. Yesterday morning, the police escorted Gu to the First Special District Court. The injured woman also勉强勉强 appeared in court to testify. Judge Feng conducted a preliminary hearing. The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, argued that the defendant had intentionally injured someone and should be severely punished. The defendant admitted to the attack but claimed that he had only used a razor. Judge Feng concluded the hearing and sentenced Gu Linsheng to eight months of imprisonment as a warning. The injured woman was helped away by her relatives.

Billboard Blown Down by Wind 141

Wound to Arm and Abdomen Proved Fatal

▲ Yang Luoying Died Wrongfully

Yang Luoying, a Cantonese man, 17 years old, resided at No. 10, Zhenghe Lane, Xinqiao Street, French Concession. At about 3:00 PM on the 5th of this month, he went out to buy books and was walking past the entrance of Rundafa Bicycle Shop at No. 2 Guangxi Road. At that time, there was a strong wind, and suddenly Rundafa's billboard was blown down, falling on Yang's body and injuring his arm and abdomen. After being injured, Yang fell to the ground in extreme pain. Constable No. 554 spotted him and immediately recorded the shop's address and sent the injured man to Renji Hospital for treatment. He also reported to the Lao Zha Police Station, instructing detectives to investigate. Yang died from his injuries at 5:00 PM the day before yesterday. The body was taken to the Felun Road morgue. Yesterday morning, a report was filed with the First Special District Court, which appointed Prosecutor Li Ying to visit the morgue and examine the body. Constable No. 554 testified that he was on duty on Guangxi Road at the time and saw a person sitting on the ground in front of the Rundafa Bicycle Shop at No. 2. He heard passersby say that the person had been injured by the shop's billboard. He summoned the shop owner, Yu Lianqing, to take the injured man to the hospital. Yang Baohua also testified that the deceased was his nephew, who lived with him. After the incident, the bicycle shop sent someone to inform him at about 5:00 PM, and he went to the hospital to check on him. He confirmed that the injured man had been struck by the billboard. Upon hearing the testimonies, the judge ruled that the deceased, a male, had indeed died from injuries to his abdomen caused by the billboard blown down by the wind. The body was handed over to Yang Baohua, the deceased's uncle, to arrange for the coffin and burial.

Inability to Make a Living Leads to Suicide 144

Zhou Yimo, a 41-year-old man from Nanjing residing at No. 720, Sanle Lane, Gordon Road, used to work as a customs broker. Due to the January 28th Incident, when Japanese troops invaded Shanghai, he was unemployed and living at home for half a year. In addition to his wife, he had six children, and the monthly expenses were enormous. Making a living was extremely difficult. Recently, he pawned almost everything he owned and was unable to find a way to make money. Therefore, he conceived the idea of death. Yesterday morning at 7:30 AM, he secretly swallowed raw opium to commit suicide. By the time his wife noticed, it was too late, and he died immediately. The police officer from Post No. 3300 arrived and transported the body to Tongren Hospital by vehicle, and then to the morgue for examination.

Civilian Ships Must Still Report In and Out 145

▲ Jianghai Customs Notice

Since the Jianghai Customs Wusong Sub-Customs was abolished last year, the Jianghai Customs Tax Affairs Department has stipulated that cargo ships traveling between Wusong and Shanghai are divided into two categories. All ships carrying more than 200 dan of cargo and holding a nationality certificate from the Navigation Administration Bureau must report to the Shanghai South Sub-Customs. Those with a capacity of less than 200 dan must report for branding and registration at the Wusong Sub-Customs at the Paotaiwan, Wusong Estuary for inspection. Since the outbreak of the war this year, this procedure has been suspended. The Jianghai Customs Tax Affairs Department, Ke Dader, feared that if civilian ships were not inspected, bandit ships would inevitably mix in and smuggle contraband, making it impossible to crack down. Therefore, he issued a notice yesterday, ordering all civilian ships to report immediately. The notice is recorded below: "Jianghai Customs General Affairs Department Notice: Regarding the matter of all civilian ships traveling to and from this port, regardless of whether they are going to sea or not, with a capacity of more than or less than 200 dan, must now be branded and registered at the Nanshi Sub-Customs or Wusong Sub-Customs. Those with a capacity of more than 200 dan will be classified as one category, and those with a capacity of less than 200 dan will be classified as another category. In the future, when entering and leaving Wusong, they must also report to the Wusong Sub-Customs for verification of the registry. All civilian ship owners are hereby notified. General Affairs Department Tax Affairs Department Ke Dader."

▲ Victim Wang Lu Has Sued the County Government

Jiangsu and Zhejiang 148

Investigation of Old Cocoons and Old Silk Completed

▲ 250,000 Bales of Old Cocoons

▲ 17,000 Dan of Old Silk

The Committee for the Reorganization of Old Factory Silk and Old Cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, after notifying silk and cocoon merchants to register the quantity of existing old cocoons and old silk, completed the first step of the work and then dispatched personnel to implement the investigation according to the planned reorganization plan. It is now learned that the investigation work has been completed. A total of 250,000 bales of old cocoons have been found, weighing 105,000 dan, which can produce about 20,000 dan of silk. Adding the existing 17,000 dan of old factory silk, the total amount of old silk is 37,000 dan. According to the government's current plan to save Chinese silk, a subsidy of 100 taels per dan for the export of old silk is required, costing 3.7 million taels of silver.

Wusong Leading Light Buoy to Be Changed 153

General Maritime Notice No. 1033 of the Maritime Department of the General Office of the General Customs Service said, "To announce the matter, the General Customs Service issued an order to check the Wusong leading light buoy belonging to Jianghai Customs. There are now places that should be changed. A separate list is required. Let the inspection and engineering company follow the instructions. With the attached list, it should be obeyed and handled. Therefore, a notice is issued and the items opened are recorded below. All Chinese and foreign shipowners are hereby notified. This is a special notice. (1) Change situation: The light is now a seventh-class lens red light constant light. It will be changed to a 290-candlepower white flashing Shuiyue electric light. In clear weather, the light can illuminate 10 nautical miles away. It flashes 50 times per minute. The light lasts for 0.4 seconds, and the extinction lasts for 0.8 seconds. (2) Function of the light buoy: The range illuminated by the light is a sector, and the two sides of the sector are 10 degrees away from the guiding route formed by the light of the buoy, the Wusong Lighthouse, and the offshore light. (3) Form of the light buoy: At high tide, the light can be 30 feet above the water surface, and the light is placed on a white steel frame. At the lower end of the light is a white disc with a diameter of 5 feet. (4) Implementation date: tentatively scheduled for around July 20 this year. No further notice will be issued at that time. (5) Location of the light buoy: still in the old location and has not changed. (6) Related books: Maritime Charts Nos. 1011, 505, 506, and 507 of the Ministry of the Navy of the Republic of China. July 6, 21st year of the Republic of China. Kanie, Inspector of Maritime Affairs Department."

Dear Editor,

Having read the news item regarding the rent exemption in Fansheng Lane in today's issue of your newspaper, it states that "the landlord, relying on being a foreign merchant, initially refused to exempt any rent, but after repeated requests from the tenants and seeing the general trend, he could not maintain a different opinion and agreed to reduce the rent for two months." Upon investigation, after the cessation of hostilities between China and Japan this year and the restoration of police authority by the Municipal Council, our office first sent a letter to the tenants of Fansheng Lane on April 12, stating that we would voluntarily exempt rent for two months. How can it be said that we "relied on being a foreign merchant and refused to exempt any rent"? This is clearly inconsistent with the facts and may cause confusion. Therefore, we have sent this letter to be published and corrected. Sincerely, to the distinguished editors of the Shanghai News Department of Shen Bao. Respectfully, Gao Yi Mansion Rental Office, July 8th.

Incoming Mail

Declaration of Initiation of the China Promotion of Civil Governance Association 169

Ma Xiangbo

As the people of our nation face successive national crises, it is the people who suffer. If the people do not save themselves, who will save them? The way to save them, in terms of the nation, lies in politics, and there is no other way. To defend against natural disasters and enemy-caused calamities, no matter who is in power or what politician it is, can they succeed without using the people's wealth and power? Can a few people plan for others and succeed, while we, the masses, cannot plan for ourselves? Therefore, based on the psychology of self-love and loyalty to self-rescue, we have created the China Promotion of Civil Governance Association and hereby reveal the key points to all compatriots:

1. Looking at the history of all nations, they all first have land and the indigenous people who live on it. The people's livelihood depends on the use of the land, and the method of using the land lies in agriculture and industry. The method of protecting the land lies in national defense, the national defense of the sea, land, and air, and the management of agriculture, animal husbandry, water, fire, construction, and forestry. Can these be competently and innovatively handled without the entire nation's participation? Therefore, historically speaking, civil governance should be used.

2. Philosophically speaking about national politics, according to the Sequence Hexagram of the Book of Changes, "There are all things, then there are men and women, husband and wife, father and son," which accumulate to form families. The reason why there must be all things is that people must rely on external things to defend and nourish their lives. According to this, it is natural human rights. Then, from families, there accumulate civilized clans and ethnic groups with etiquette, hierarchy, and civilization. Every inch of land and every individual is defended by the nation's financial resources, and all must fight with the same hatred to achieve victory, like King Tang's campaign against Chou Xiang, seeking revenge for ordinary men and women. However, the collection of people's wealth and the requisition of people's labor, which is the people's lives, can only be carried out by the sovereign power stipulated in the national constitution. It cannot be forcibly seized and manipulated by one person, one family, one party, or one class. To do so is what Mencius called acting unjustly and killing the innocent. This greatly violates justice. The people should, based on justice, restore their right to self-governance and constitutionalism. If this is presented to the people of the world, there will be no denial.

(To be continued)

Page 17

Free Talk

Sayings of Old Man Jiu Wang, Ma Xiangbo

Mr. Ma's Views 170

—

Speaking of the theory of evolution, there is actually nothing extraordinary about it. We have long known Darwin's theory of survival of the fittest: big insects eat small insects, the strong swallow the weak. Everyone is accustomed to it, but we just haven't systematized these facts.

In ancient China, there were also many thinkers about spontaneous generation. For example, Zhuangzi is a representative of Chinese evolution theory. Zhuangzi's book once recorded:

(Zhuang Zhou dreamed of becoming a butterfly, a butterfly fluttering happily! Did he know that he was content or not? Did he not know that he was Zhou? Suddenly he awoke, and he was abruptly Zhou! Did Zhou dream of becoming a butterfly, or did the butterfly dream of becoming Zhou? Zhou and the butterfly must have a distinction. This is called "the transformation of things." (See Zhuangzi, Inner Chapters, Wandering Freely)

Zhuangzi indulged in wild thoughts, becoming a butterfly in a dream, saying it was "the transformation of things." It was originally naive and mysteriously laughable. However, isn't it equally laughable to Western evolutionists who believe that humans evolved from monkeys!

Similar to the idea of "humans evolved from monkeys," there is also a passage in Zhuangzi's Chapter on Supreme Happiness:

(There is seed, which becomes a Qi when it gets water. When it gets the juncture of water and earth, it becomes the clothing of a poisonous clam. When it grows on a mound, it becomes lingxie. When lingxie gets a lush place, it becomes blackfoot. The root of blackfoot becomes a grub. Its leaf becomes a butterfly. The butterfly, Xuye, transforms and becomes an insect, which lives under the stove. Its shape is like shedding, and its name is quzhuo. The quzhuo of a chick becomes a bird in a thousand days, and its name is ganyu gu. The foam of ganyu gu becomes simi. Simi becomes vinegar. Yi Lu is born from vinegar. Huang Ni is born from Jiu You. Mao Rui is born from rotten Quan. Yang Xi is like Bu Zhi Jiu bamboo, producing Qing Ning. Qing Ning produces Cheng. Cheng produces horses. Horses produce humans. Humans then return to the machine. All things come from the machine, and all things enter the machine.)

Zhuangzi's theory of evolution is more mysterious, more thorough, and more intense than Darwin's theory of evolution! Darwin's theory of evolution says that humans evolved from monkeys; Zhuangzi says that humans evolved from horses. Then, isn't Zhuangzi's theory of evolution more mysterious? Zhuangzi not only said "horses produce humans," but also went backwards, even saying "there is seed," isn't that more thorough and more intense than Darwin's "Origin of Species"? However, monkeys are monkeys, horses are horses, and humans are humans. Facts tell us that things each have their own species, truly "not related at all."

Epitaph for the Martyrdom of My Brother's Wife, Madam Ma, in the National Crisis 171

— Tang Wenzhi

In the spring of the Ren Shen year, the Japanese attacked Shanghai. My Nineteenth Route Army, led by Cai Tingkai and others, resisted them. After more than a month of stalemate, the enemy landed from Liuhe and Yanglin in my county. Our army retreated to Loucheng. The enemy followed, dropping bombs from airplanes like rain. My clan brother Wenquan's wife, Madam Ma, was ill and unable to get up. She was killed by a bomb in Beihou Alley, north of the North City. Her body and bed were thrown into the neighboring house. At that time, Wenquan was serving in the army in Jiangxi. Her elder brothers Wen Shou and Wen Cui had already separated from her. At this time, they fled into the countryside. Two days later, she was finally laid to rest. Everyone who saw or heard of it was saddened. Three months later, her husband's elder brother, Wenzhi, respectfully recorded the matter in the family records and wrote an inscription with tears. My brother's wife's surname was Ma, given name Xienan, daughter of Ma Guren, a scholar of Songjiang. Her mother was Madam Xu. She became an orphan at the age of three and lived with her uncle, Xu Bicheng. She successively studied at the Suzhou Girls' School and the Wulou Zhengze School. At the age of twenty, she came to marry into my Tang family as the fourth wife of Jiting Gong. She served her parents-in-law with utmost filial piety. Wenquan traveled and lived abroad, and she always went with him. They endured hardships and separation and never had a day of rest. She gave birth to eight children, five of whom died young. Those who survived were her daughter Qinghong and her sons Qingzhuo and Qingfu. At the time of my brother's wife's death, Qinghong and Qingzhuo were by her side. They heard the sound of airplanes rattling around the corner of the house and hurriedly told the children to go to the front building to avoid them. Suddenly, there was a loud crash. The ground cracked and the sky collapsed. The building tilted. My brother's wife passed away. Her mother, Madam Xu, was pressed under the stove. Qinghong and Qingzhuo were terrified. They jumped down from the window and ran out the door. Soldiers blocked the road. Qingzhuo cried for help. A soldier took him away. It was not until the next day that he was able to return. Qinghong ran in panic to the Yulou School and saw a military officer climbing over the wall. She knelt down and cried, "My mother is dead! My grandmother still has sounds of calling. Please go and save her!" The military officer then led soldiers to drag Madam Xu out of the rubble. She fainted and was revived. Qingfu was being cared for by a wet nurse in the countryside. It was not until a month later that he was found. Alas, alas. Peace came only at the summer solstice. We then set up an altar and performed the ceremony. Alas, my brother's wife was a weak woman who studied and understood great righteousness. She could not wield weapons to defend the country. She only suffered a tragic end due to her frail health. Her mother, alone and helpless, was overwhelmed with grief. If the spirits in the afterlife know, they will not rest in peace. The responsibility for the calamity of Zha Yang does not belong to anyone but me. The inscription reads:

Since ancient times, good warfare has been subjected to heavenly punishment. What comes out of you returns to you. Blessings and calamities are divided between good and evil. How could one expect to suffer disaster without cause? The flying bird casts a shadow, leaving an ominous sound. The shaking house hides families in the dimness. Ascending to heaven and entering the earth is a difficult and righteous task. I grieve for my brother's wife, whose righteous deeds are fragrant, sacrificing her life for the glory of the country. Thunder and lightning hide the darkness with fortitude. Suddenly, the tears well up as I gaze. I cannot bear to leave this high hall. I pity these young children who are dying. My eyes reach thousands of miles, my heart is wounded in spring. The waters of Loujiang flow forever, vast and boundless.

World Miscellany 172

— Hai Ke

A Wooden Leg as a Safe. A poor woman in England was admitted to an American hospital due to illness, requesting free treatment. She stayed for five years, receiving very careful treatment from the doctors. Unexpectedly, just as the treatment was about to be completed, it was discovered that her wooden prosthetic leg was actually a safe deposit box inside a bank, containing 650 British pounds in cash, equivalent to more than 6,500 Mexican silver dollars. As a result, the hospital filed a lawsuit, demanding that this woman who pretended to be poor pay for medical and hospital expenses, calculated at one gold dollar per day, for a total of five years. This amount is also considerable.

Similar cases of hoarding cash are not uncommon. There was a female miser who hid money in various parts of her house, one thousand here, ten thousand there. Even she herself couldn't keep track. Later, she died, and her descendants had to accept her inheritance. They had to completely demolish the house to search for it one by one.

According to surveys, the total amount of gold hidden in Britain is about 400 million British pounds in cash or banknotes. Many people hide it in unimaginable places and it never circulates. According to some economists, the decline in the global economic situation is partly due to these cash-hoarding misers.

Vow to Launch the Northern Expedition, Wounds of the Past and Present 173

— Zizai

Today marks exactly six full years since the National Revolutionary Army vowed to launch the Northern Expedition. On July 9, 1926, the Revolutionary Army vowed its oath at the East Campus in Guangzhou. The ceremony was grand, and the military appearance was magnificent. On that day, more than 20,000 people from the Navy, Army, Gendarmerie, and Whampoa Military Academy students arrived. Wu Zhihui, representing the Central Party Headquarters, presented the flag, which read, "Implement the overthrow of the warlords, tools of imperialism." Chiang Kai-shek bowed and accepted it. At that time, the people of the whole country were suffering from the oppression of warlords and the invasion of powerful neighbors. They yearned for the success of the Revolutionary Army's Northern Expedition very much. Therefore, it set out to Hunan, recovered Wuhan in October, and stabilized the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. In the spring of 1927, it recovered the provinces in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River. In the spring of 1928, it continued the Northern Expedition and recovered Beijing in June, unifying the country. It has been six full years since then. Looking around at the situation in which the people of the whole country find themselves, there is the oppression of imperialists from the outside, and the instigation of the remaining warlords from the inside. Years of civil war, bandits everywhere, and repeated disasters have plunged the people into misery. Thinking about it quietly, one cannot help but sigh.

In the past six years, foreign affairs and domestic politics have been unbearable to look back on. Excerpts from the Central Party Headquarters' declaration of departure on that day are compared with today's reality. Is there a difference? There is no difference, and it is even more severe. (The plight of the Chinese people has reached its extreme today. Speaking of farmers, the fruits of their blood and sweat are entirely used to supply the looting of soldiers and bandits. The pre-collection of special taxes has increased endlessly. Hard work all year round does not bring enough to eat. Selling fields and cattle has gradually led to unemployment. Wherever soldiers and bandits pass, villages are reduced to ruins. The old and weak die in ditches, and the young are mostly captured. Men are treated as cattle and horses, and women are raped. Speaking of workers, they work all day long, and the fruits of their labor can only barely sustain their lives. They have no surplus and no security. Usually, they are always in danger of losing their jobs. When disaster strikes, they cannot help but fall into the ranks of vagrants. Speaking of merchants, they are oppressed from the outside by foreign merchants selling foreign goods and transporting local goods, and from the inside by the heavy taxes and miscellaneous levies and blatant extortion of large and small warlords and bandits. Bankruptcies are common. Speaking of the intellectual class, teachers are always worried about their salaries being overdue, unable to transmit their wisdom. Students are often plagued by banditry, cutting off their resources and unable to advance their studies. Schools are closed due to the fires of war every year. Elementary school teachers have become coolies. Others, such as the soldiers under the command of warlords in various provinces, are mostly farmers and workers who have joined the army to seek a living. However, after joining the army, not only is there still no guarantee of a livelihood, but they are also driven to their deaths by ambitious warlords. Their good blood is not used to pacify the country and save the people, but rather to kill the people for the sake of the warlords' support, to fight for fame and wealth for the warlords. What is more tragic than this?). (Omitted below)

Alas, although the times are six years apart, the situation is no different from the past. Looking around, the country is fragmented, and it is unbearable to mention the painful things again. In addition, the Northeast has fallen, and the map has changed color. Guangdong, the source of the revolution, is willing to engage in civil war at this time of national crisis, but shrinks back from resisting foreign aggression. Revolutionary soldiers have been reduced to this. Reflecting on the past and present, one cannot help but sigh deeply.

Twenty Years Ago's Hatred of Heaven (Below) 174

— Tianhen

National subjugation, racial extinction, partition – all people across the nation have heard of it and known it for a long time. But it was not expected that crises would continue to erupt, and the danger of national subjugation and racial extinction would become even more imminent. Internal worries and external troubles intersect and encroach upon each other. The Republic of China is in danger, alas, in great danger.

The Three Eastern Provinces are the Three Eastern Provinces of the Chinese people, but they cannot be the Three Eastern Provinces of China. The terms "South Manchuria" and "North Manchuria" are simply a map delineating the partition of my Three Eastern Provinces by Japan and Russia. South of Harbin is the sphere of influence of the Japanese. No, it is the territory of the Japanese. North of Harbin is the sphere of influence of the Russians. No, it is also the territory of the Russians. But it was not expected that it would not only be a sphere of influence or a territory, but even the right of residence of the Chinese people has been taken away. This is truly not treating us Chinese people as human beings. What is tolerable, what is not tolerable?

Oh, my people, are my people really going to sit by and watch the Japanese and Russians insult and humiliate us, causing our country to fall into death? The Republic of China, the Republic of China exchanged for by force, and it is actually powerless to deal with violent neighbors? Do my people not all have the heart of "rather die than live without freedom"? If we do not quickly devise a method of resistance and confrontation, my people will only die. Rather than sitting and waiting to die as slaves, it is better to die in battle as brave ghosts. When I look at the flag of three colors, I only think of seeking the blue sky and white sun in red blood. Alas.)

The Chinese Revolution has been going on for twenty years, and Mr. Dai Jitao has also become one of the important figures in the central government, jointly wielding the power of governance. However, the weakness of the national situation is even worse than before, and there is a lament that it is getting worse every day. Throughout the Qing Dynasty and after sixteen years of rule by the warlord government, the name of Manchuria as Chinese territory could still be preserved, but it cannot be preserved after the success of the revolution. This is something that none of the giants of the people's party and Mr. Jitao could have expected. When Mr. Jitao was a newspaper reporter, Manchuria was only under the intangible control of Japan and Russia, and he still issued dangerous words to awaken the people, saying that rather than sitting and waiting to die as slaves, it is better to die in battle as brave ghosts. Now that he holds the power of national governance, he can carry out his ambitions. However, he has remained silent. For the past nine months, all that has been heard is that he has initiated the establishment of a secret Buddhist Golden Light Dao Field in the Yonghe Temple in Beiping, passively praying to quell the chaos, and wanting to rely on boundless Buddhist Dharma to shift the calamity. Compared with the positivism of twenty years ago, he is like two different people. Writing this far, I can only end my article with Mr. Jitao's own words: "Alas." What else can I say? What else can I say?

A Discussion of the Nail-Making Industry 175

— Huasheng

Wire nails, known in the West as Wire Nails, are commonly known as "foreign nails." According to historical records, imported foreign nails were originally invented in France. Their import into our country was also earliest from France. Therefore, foreign nails are also called "French nails." In 1880, Germany and France began to transport and sell these products to the United States. Because they met the needs of the people of that country, those who engaged in this business once held a temporary monopoly. By 1917, the United States was able to manufacture 17 million barrels of the same nails itself. By 1927, this had increased to more than 29 million barrels. From the quantity of products, one can imagine the scale of the equipment. There are also more than 30 nail factories of various sizes in Japan. The two largest are attached to state-run steel mills, producing more than 1,000 barrels of wire nails per day. Statistics show that the annual output of nails in Japan is about 3 million barrels. In addition to a small number of sales to Nanyang and various provinces in Northeast China, the rest is for domestic use. Due to their high quality and high price, American-made large quantities of wire nails are not easily sold in foreign markets.

In the past ten years, Chinese people have advocated domestic products, and the call has been loud. Various machine-made Western-style goods have sprung up like mushrooms, and wire nails have emerged in response to the needs of the times.

After the revolution, Hubei had a Hanyang Needle and Nail Factory. Unfortunately, it closed down before any goods were shipped. According to research, the first successful imitation in our country was Mr. Huang Shifu of the Shanghai Gongqin Iron Factory. All the nail-making machines, large and small, in the factory were designed and manufactured by itself. It now produces 15,000 barrels of nails per month, making it the leader among nail factories in this port. There are now nine other nail factories, both Chinese and foreign, large and small, with a total monthly output of 40,000 to 50,000 barrels, which is sufficient to meet the needs of the whole country. Therefore, in recent years, the import of foreign nails, except for the provinces in the Northeast, has been almost entirely replaced by domestic products. The result of Gongqin Factory's ten years of hard work has somewhat supplemented the people's livelihood.

Shaoxing Summer Cocoons Have an Extremely High Waste Rate 192

▲ An average of 350 catties of fresh cocoons are needed to produce 100 catties of dried cocoons: Due to the poor spring cocoon harvest and extremely low cocoon prices this year, farmers in various cities and villages in Shaoxing suffered significant losses. Therefore, few people raised summer silkworms. Only those with mulberry leaves at home reduced the amount of silkworm eggs they hatched. However, the weather was terrible, no different from the spring silkworm season. Continuous moldy rain and abnormal temperatures caused many silkworm ants to be abandoned. The cocoon production only reached 20% of previous years, and the cocoons were damp, with mostly thin-skinned and double-shelled cocoons. The waste rate was extremely high. Because the villagers had nowhere to sell their cocoons, they mostly dried and reeled them themselves. It is said that the average waste rate is 350 catties of fresh cocoons to produce 100 catties of dried cocoons.

Wuxun Tea Market Falls into the Same Predicament 194

▲Wuyuan: Wuyuan's Zi tea production, with its tender and delicate leaves, was superior to previous years. The tea merchants also considered the quality to be excellent and worth acquiring. Various tea companies transported large quantities of Zhenmei and Huase boxed tea, accumulating to a massive ten thousand boxes. Therefore, tea merchants saw no hope for a turnaround in the tea market and were hesitant to invest in this Zhen tea. Mountain households, due to low closing prices, also stopped picking tea one after another. Yesterday, the price of new tea from the Beiyuan tea mountains plummeted to forty yuan, following the market's collapse. Tea companies with smaller purchases have gradually closed their operations in recent days, and the market situation is rapidly deteriorating.

▲Tunxi: Due to the Shanghai market's continued decline, Tunxi tea companies have mostly ceased purchasing tea. Previously, various tea merchants, anticipating growing demand from tea companies, transported twice as much new tea as before, accumulating to a massive ten thousand dan. Currently, high-quality Zhuang tea is priced at fifty yuan, medium-quality at forty yuan, and low-quality at just over twenty yuan. However, tea companies are finding it difficult to sell, so despite the loose prices at the warehouses, they dare not purchase any more. Even the tea sellers in flourishing shops with the highest quality goods, are seeing their wares pile up and are seeing prices fall back to twenty-four yuan, as buyers are already sated. The market is becoming increasingly bleak.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Japanese Foreign Vice Minister's Gaffe 198

— Buddha

China United Press, Tokyo, 6th: Japanese Foreign Vice Minister Arita, stated to the British ambassador the other day that the Japanese government would not unilaterally recognize Manchukuo before the Lytton Commission returned to Geneva to report. This matter was discovered by the Japanese warlords, who were greatly angered and attacked him vehemently, making it difficult for him to keep his position. This statement, in normal eyes, was not a mistake or even a simple fact, but in the eyes of the Japanese warlords, it was a great loss of face. Because in the eyes of the Japanese warlords, the League of Nations was not important. They were constantly talking about withdrawing from the League of Nations, but now Arita said that he would not unilaterally recognize it before the Lytton report, which made it clear that the Japanese still had some misgivings about the League of Nations. It was indeed a slip of the tongue.

If that's the case, then diplomats can never tell the truth. It's the golden rule of diplomats. I don't mean to praise the effectiveness of our diplomats. No matter how diplomatically unsuccessful they are, the people will repeatedly ask them to reveal the truth and policy of diplomacy. They always refuse to change their tune, and their official responses are all about victory and success. They never say a word of truth. So, after repeated negotiations, victory always belongs to us. This is a proud situation.

Moreover, not only our diplomats are like this, but also every politician. Generally, once they become officials, they never tell the truth. Today a speech, tomorrow a declaration, are all described vividly, but the result is a slippery check. Now it has become even more advanced. The so-called speeches do not necessarily require people to ask about them. A speech-style news report is already taken out of their pockets. This is a convenient and time-saving thing.

Therefore, our country is completely a diplomatic country. No matter what happens, it is not easy for the people to know the truth. This is probably still the mental method passed down by Confucius: the people can be made to follow it, but they cannot be made to understand it.

Literature

Missing the Best Time 199

— Sung Tuo Using a Familiar Tune

Composed in a Guest House during the Wusong Anti-Japanese War when Reinforcements Failed to Arrive

Swallows sing and orioles warble. In the clear day, the curtain is rolled up. The red pavilion is weary of embroidery. The clouds and duckweed drift to the horizon. Who cares about people's sorrow? Gazing wistfully at the beginning of spring, until the end of spring, I vainly shed tears on the red mud. Truly, my longing is enough.

Li Ting Yan (Feeling Inspired when Passing Zhabei in the Late Spring of Ren Shen Year) 200

Gazing wistfully at Jiangnan, the misty rain is still the same. Fallen flowers have no owner. Who is living in the deep courtyard? No one is seen. It deceived the parrot in front of the curtain. The pavilions and terraces of last year have been replaced by red dust and yellow earth. Lonely tides return to the Jiangpu. The mountains are cut off and clouds will fill the gap. Catkins gather into balls, and the sky is getting late. I am afraid to speak of the wind's madness like a tiger. Let's not talk about the many rises and falls, and the singing and dancing in the red buildings.

Qing Yu An (Seeing off the Spring at Songbin) 201

The river waves sway with green and the peaks lie horizontally with emerald. I am afraid to bring up sad things. A glance reveals a strange landscape. Cuckoos sing and orioles trill. Willows sleep and flowers slumber. They are all tears of longing. This catastrophe has come for no reason. It seems that this Jiangshan has been overrun by Hu cavalry. Fragrant grass and setting sun, spring is leaving. The bells in the empty temple easily sound and the tides scold like reproaches. The poet is determined to be drunk.

Science

Lithographic Printing 202

— Bing Er

The art of lithographic printing was invented by the German, Senefelder, in 1799. This lithographic stone contains the main component of calcium carbonate, which is different from ordinary lithographic stone. The surface of the lithographic stone is very smooth, and its texture is composed of fine particles, with very small holes in between. The function is to absorb moisture. These small holes cannot be seen with the naked eye without a microscope. The source of lithographic stone is in Solnhofen, Germany. Before it was discovered that this stone could be used for printing, it was completely used for paving roads. After knowing the function of this stone, the area, which was originally a barren area, has been transformed into a wealthy area, and the area can also be called the only place in the world that produces lithographic stone.

The area of ​​lithographic stone commonly used is rectangular, with a thickness of about three or four inches. In addition to being able to absorb moisture, the ingredients in the lithographic stone can be combined with fatty soaps. Once combined, it can absorb ink. If Arabic gum is applied to the stone surface, it cannot absorb oil. Therefore, if you want to print multi-color pictures, in addition to coloring, the blank areas are subjected to the chemical action of this gum, and the ink can be removed, and the printing can be satisfactory.

In the printing method, text or other patterns are written on tracing paper with fatty ink (tracing paper is not the commonly used blue tracing paper, but a transparent tracing paper similar to the original paper). It is placed upside down on the lithographic stone, and after moistening it with a damp cloth, the machine is turned to press it, and the text appears on the lithographic stone. Then remove the paper, and after slightly modifying the printed words, the object can be printed, or the fatty ink can be directly written on the stone surface. However, this is more difficult, because writing upside down is not as satisfactory as writing on tracing paper and pressing it on the lithographic stone.

In addition to the above two printing methods, it can also be printed as a lithograph in this way. After moistening the picture with water, a zinc plate coated with chromium photosensitive material is placed and put it in a filter and exposed to sunlight for ten minutes. After it is photosensitive, take out the zinc plate, roll the entire plate with an ink roller, bake it slightly on the fire, and then wash it lightly with thin cotton dipped in clean water. Then, the unexposed chromium colloids are dissolved by water together with the ink oil, and the exposed text or image part can resist moisture and absorb ink oil. The shadow remains on the zinc plate, and there is no danger of shadow loss. Then, cover it with tracing paper and roll it with an ink oil roller, and sprinkle rosin powder, plus a liquid made of nitric acid and agar. This is to prevent its fatty lines from becoming thick and green, and it can be printed out.

The printing method has been described above. After use, the ink marks on the lithographic stone cannot be removed. To remove them, you can wipe them with turpentine or pumice powder. The printing color can be from one color to more than ten colors.

A Brilliant Female Physiognomist 203

— Flood

A section chief from the XX Department came to Shanghai specifically to see the devastation after the war. He was staying in a very beautiful room at Yipinxiang. I went to visit him around 7 o'clock in the afternoon.

"Are you busy tonight? If you are busy, then tomorrow..." After a few polite greetings, he said this.

"After a long separation, we should talk more even if we are busy, let alone if we are not." Although I agreed to him in this way, I always felt that his somewhat abrupt question was a polite request for me to leave.

"Sir! The physiognomists are here!" The waiter suddenly pushed the door in and said with a joyful smile, as if he was reporting good news.

"This! Uh! Please let them in!" Then he turned his head and said to me, "It's nothing, I just asked some physiognomists to come and have some fun!"

A crisp sound of leather shoes sounded. Good heavens! It turned out to be two fairy-like modern girls! Where were the prophets with tall crowns and wide belts that I had expected? Their faces were covered with lead powder and rouge, thick lipstick was applied to their lips, and the rose essence sprinkled on their heads dripped down, instantly filling the room with fragrance. Their gossamer-like gauze faintly revealed their delicate, tender white breasts, soft, flexible bellies, and coy buttocks. I had already very sensibly moved to sit on the edge of the bed, so that they could get closer to tell fortunes.

"Sir! You really have a good face! Your forehead is full, your jaw is square, and your nose..." One of the fatter girls said, moving her two small, bright red lips as she spoke.

"Your dragon and tiger are in proportion, your palms are as soft as cotton, and plus this red seal and the straight life line, it indicates that you will be rich and noble..." Another palm reader said. She was slender and always had a gentle smile on her face.

Although they read faces and palms differently, their expressions were almost the same. For example, they talked while smiling, and they pointed while talking! That is, they were touching. The beauty of their whole secret and magic, all in these small, clever movements, smiles, faces, and a different scene appeared on the twinkling eyes.

As an outsider, although I appeared very generous in listening to their high-level instructions, the fear in my heart was beating faster and faster; not to mention him who let them touch his fingers and face, even if he were a clay sculpture or a wooden carving, he would inevitably be charmed. And in fact, he was always staring at them with rapt attention, and it seemed that he was telling their fortunes. Later, they even stopped speaking, and only six eyes looked at each other silently!

"Ahem!" I coughed, clearing my throat, breaking the silence and tension that had lasted for a long time.

"Sorry!" He smiled and gave each of them ten yuan!

"Thank you! Sir, you are so kind!" They left the room in a victorious manner. Then I asked him how he knew these two brilliant female physiognomists as soon as he got off the bus. He gave me a colorful advertisement. What caught my eye were the two girls' animated photos, with the words:

Ms. XX and Ms. XX are the most famous female physiognomists in Shanghai! If you want to invite them to come and tell your fortune, whether it is in a hotel, restaurant, brothel, wine shop, or any public place, send an invitation and they will come. If you are afraid of being delayed, call us. If you favor us with your presence, you are especially welcome. We have a quiet fortune-telling room for your private conversation! The fortune-telling fee is two yuan, and there is no extra charge for going out. Phone number XX, XX Hotel.

Casual Chat

Summer 204

— Yi Ping

If spring is like Greta Garbo's mystery, then summer is Clara Bow's madness.

○　○　○　○

On every relatively busy pedestrian street, there are ice cream stalls. It is said that the health bureau is trying its best to ban these unhygienic seasonal foods, but as long as you donate a letter, you can shout and sell loudly, which is not contradictory to the ambulance with the Red Cross giving vaccinations everywhere.

○　○　○　○

"Another 50% off! Eliminate enemy goods! Relieve silk!" The newspaper published such a big advertisement; although it was declared to be enemy goods, the butterfly-like girls returned with large bags and small bags. Cheap goods are always attractive to everyone.

○　○　○　○

The night in the French Park is full of seduction. Many poets and novelists use its background as the moment when the protagonists in their books complete a kiss.

Mysterious night, especially summer night. The cool breeze gathers through the gaps in the trees. Under the faint light, the fragrant traces of ladies are everywhere. In the darkness, many evils occur. Temporary revelry, lifetime regret!

Night, mysterious night! Summer, mad summer!

○　○　○　○

Stepping on the North Sichuan Road Bridge, the scars of the war cannot cover the sadness in my heart, but if you walk slowly, the music in the silver cafe, the temptation of the flesh, and the stimulation of alcohol, have made you forget in your drunken heart that this is a mysterious street that has been ravaged by imperialism.

Two shadows appear from the darkness and disappear into the darkness. What remains in my mind is the fluffy hair and the cheongsam fluttering in the wind.

○　○　○　○

(Summer) has laid barbed wire to capture the poor prisoners. The reports of (rape) (murder) (poison) (heat) record his achievements.

Bulletin Board

Jiangsu High Court Second Branch 205

▲Criminal Judgment: In the opium appeal case of Lin Xiang and others, the original judgment on the crimes and penalties of Lin Xiang, Liang Jinchu, and Chen Zhangshi, and the confiscation of property, were all revoked. Lin Xiang, Liang Jinchu, and Chen Zhangshi were each sentenced to six months of imprisonment and fined one hundred yuan for helping to sell opium.

▲In the case of Zheng Shihao and others endangering the Republic of China, He Rongxuan was sentenced to five years of imprisonment for organizing a group with the aim of endangering the Republic of China. Zheng Shihao, Zhang Mingzhe, Wang Yongkang, Zhao Guibao, Wang Faming, Lin Qi, and Wu Chan were all found not guilty.

▲Shanghai Municipal Council sues Yang Xiaosizi for theft. The original judgment was revoked. Yang Xiaosizi was sentenced to one year of imprisonment for joint theft.

▲Public Notice: In the appeal case of Puyi Real Estate Company versus Mao Mi'er for rent arrears, the court has now scheduled a public hearing for 8:30 am on July 19. This public notice is issued to the respondent, Mao Mi'er.

▲Civil Ruling: In the protest case of Deng Zhongze versus Deng Wenhai regarding the request to exchange the previously provided guarantee bonds and other matters in the dispute over property division, the protest was rejected, and the protest fee was to be borne by the protester.

▲In the appeal case of Shi Xilin and others versus Wang Huiqing regarding compensation and debt repayment, the original judgment concerning Shi Xilin's compensation of six thousand taels of silver to Wang Huiqing and the litigation costs was changed to the first and second instance litigation costs being borne by Wang Huiqing. (Above are July 7th)

Shanghai First Special District Local Court 206

▲Criminal First Instance Judgement: Yu Taotao guilty of embezzlement, sentenced to two months imprisonment; Jin Xiaozhang not guilty.▲Fan Ronggen guilty of one count of theft, sentenced to two months imprisonment.▲Li Asan, repeat offender for theft, sentenced to five months imprisonment.▲Xia Deqiang, guilty of three counts of armed robbery with accomplices, sentenced to seven years imprisonment for each count, total execution of eight years; Zhu Hegen, Chen Ziqing, Yao Fuyuan, guilty of three counts of armed robbery with accomplices, sentenced to seven years imprisonment for each count, each executing seven years.▲Wang Afa, guilty of attempted robbery, sentenced to four months imprisonment.▲Jiang Hongsheng, repeat offender for attempted robbery, sentenced to three years imprisonment.▲Lü A'gen, repeat offender for extortion, sentenced to two years imprisonment; not guilty on the charge of extorting Li Chunqing; Nie Yongxing not guilty.▲Li Qiwei, Zhang Xinqian, each sentenced to two months imprisonment and fined 200 yuan for using currency with reduced weight.▲Gong Haiyun sentenced to one year imprisonment and fined 100 yuan for providing premises for opium smoking with intent to profit; Shen Lansheng, repeat offender for opium smoking, sentenced to four months imprisonment and fined 80 yuan.▲Yao Daofu sentenced to one month imprisonment for opium smoking.▲Su Asan's lawsuit against Shi Guifu not accepted.▲Zheng Ziqian not guilty on the charge of selling opium substitutes; fined 300 yuan for possessing opium paraphernalia for criminal use; Cui Daoquan not guilty.▲Sun Xiaoerzi and Chen Da'wanzi, each sentenced to three years and six months imprisonment for armed robbery with accomplices.▲Jiang Abao sentenced to three months imprisonment for theft.▲Zhang Ruiyuan found not guilty in the assault case.▲Sun Jinlang, repeat offender for theft, sentenced to four months imprisonment for each of three counts, total execution of six months.▲Shen Wenxiang sentenced to two months imprisonment for theft.▲Zhu Ada, repeat offender for theft, sentenced to four months imprisonment.▲Du Youhai, Wang Yingguang, and Liu Gu'shi each sentenced to two months imprisonment for smoking opium substitutes; Shi A'er sentenced to one month imprisonment for smoking opium substitutes.

▲Civil First Instance Judgement: You Heng Real Estate Company versus Ma Xiaodi for rent arrears; the defendant shall repay the plaintiff 360 yuan in rent and vacate the premises; the defendant shall bear the litigation costs; the eviction portion of this case is subject to immediate execution.▲Le Langsheng versus Liu Fukang et al. for loan arrears; the defendant Liu Fukang shall repay the plaintiff 600 yuan; if unable to repay, the defendants Weng Wansen, Zhang Youlin, and Qiang Boying shall be jointly and severally liable for repayment; the defendant Liu Fukang shall bear the litigation costs.▲Wan Chang Rice Shop Lu Congtang versus Xi Junping for compensation; the plaintiff's claim is dismissed; the plaintiff shall bear the litigation costs.▲Shen Daxin versus Pan Jiasheng for loan arrears; the defendant shall repay the plaintiff 100 yuan; the defendant shall bear the litigation costs.▲Lu Junyao versus Xu Guiwen for goods arrears; the defendant Xu Guiwen shall repay the plaintiff 39 yuan; the defendant Cao Deyun shall repay the plaintiff 21 yuan; the defendants shall bear the litigation costs proportionally.

▲Criminal Instructions: Sang Wangshi is an opium offender; her father, Wang Hongbing, is ill in prison; a petition requests permission for bail to suspend execution; upon reviewing the petition and the prison doctor's examination, the offender's current condition is quite good, and there is no threat to her life during imprisonment; the request is denied.▲Zhu Rongqing requests the suspension of detention and bail for Zhu Shouqing; upon reviewing the petition, the case has been adjudicated, and the requests for suspension of detention and bail are difficult to grant.▲Lawyer Huang Jue petitions on behalf of Li Chenghun for the retrieval of evidence in the Deng Zhongze fraud case, a deposit slip from Fuan Insurance Company; upon reviewing the petition, Li Chenghun is directed to provide proper surety and then proceed with the claim.

▲Civil Instructions: Zhang Zhongbao versus Xu Yisan for mortgage arrears; a petition requests execution; the debtor is ordered to submit the arrears to the court within seven days.▲Daxin Dye Factory Que Pingzhi versus Jiang Guanhua for arrears; a petition requests execution; the debtor is ordered to pay the arrears to the court within five days; the petitioner is instructed to submit proof of management records for review.▲Gai Jiasheng versus Zhang Yiwen for loan arrears; a petition requests dismissal of the case; the dismissal is granted.▲Shenglatelem versus Jing Sixi for loan arrears; a continued petition requests execution; the matter will be investigated.▲Zhang Decheng Shop versus Zhang Hongqing for loan arrears; a petition requests execution; the case file has not yet been returned by the Third Instance Court; the request is temporarily deferred.▲Shen Laosan versus Cai Quanfu for arrears; a petition requests execution; the case has already been appealed on June 11th; the request is temporarily deferred.▲Heiertesheng versus Zhou Awu et al. for loan arrears; a petition requests execution; the case has not been finalized; the request is temporarily deferred.▲Daxing Material Company et al. regarding the pre-judgment attachment of goods arrears case versus Miao Yaochu; a petition requests the lifting of the attachment; the court will review the case upon the creditor's petition.▲Lu Di petitions for execution regarding the arrears case versus Pi Limaoman; the case will be summoned for execution.▲Dai Xiaorong petitions for the issuance of an arrest warrant regarding the goods arrears case versus Dai Tingsheng; the issuance of an arrest warrant for pursuit and collection is ordered.▲Jiang Zuotang petitions for execution regarding the loan arrears case versus Ye Lansheng et al.; continued summons and collection are ordered.▲Shadusheng petitions for execution regarding the debt arrears case versus Xu Qing et al.; the court will issue a summons and pursue the matter.▲Taili Company petitions for the purchase of auctioned items regarding the rent arrears case versus Xu Hongxing; the auction shall be announced according to law.▲Su Yangshi petitions for execution regarding the alimony case versus Su Shoutian et al.; continued summons and collection are ordered.▲Dong Lingfa et al. regarding the priority claim versus Xie Chengji; request to examine the case, as it is not yet finalized; the case file has not been returned by the higher court, and therefore cannot be speculated upon; the party is instructed to petition the clerk of the higher court in accordance with the law.▲Zhao Yunzhong offers surety for the pre-judgment attachment of goods embezzlement case versus Gu Ruofeng; the amount of the security must comply with the pre-judgment attachment ruling before it can be reviewed; the request to provide surety is denied.▲Shenchang Foreign Firm petitions for assistance in execution regarding the goods arrears case versus Tiantai Foreign Firm; the request is approved, and the previously issued certificate must be submitted to the court for verification.▲Miao Yaochu petitions for the removal of the pre-judgment attachment and the retrieval of the security deposit regarding the goods arrears case versus Daxing Material Company et al.; the request is approved; the lifting of the attachment and storage of the case file are ordered; the security deposit must be reported and retrieved at the court on the morning of the 16th of this month at 9:00 AM.▲Guoen continues to request the issuance of a mandate to manage the estate of the deceased Qiu Yeshaluomen; upon review of the petition and attachments, management of the estate is not merely simple administration and should be determined by the existence of inheritance rights; the deceased Qiu Yeshaluomen was of Iraqi nationality; how is inheritance law determined under Iraqi law, and can the petitioner inherit the estate under that law? The court has no basis to determine this, and the request to issue a mandate to manage the estate is not approved; the submitted documents will be returned.
